<dsc reserve="868" >This model is an XDE model template for the RUP Analysis Model.

The Analysis Model is where the Analysis Classes and analysis Use-Case Realizations reside.  It serves as an abstraction of the Design Model.

Note: Whether or not a separate Analysis Model and Design Model should be maintained is a project-specific decision.  If a separate Analysis Model is created, but not maintained, then the Analysis Classes will be moved into the appropriate Design Model partition and refined.  Another option is to simply create the Analysis Classes and analysis Use-Case Realizations in the Design Model and then evolve them into their design form from there.

In this template, the Analysis Model has been partitioned into two packages: &quot;Analysis Elements&quot; and &quot;Analysis Use-Case Realizations&quot;.  View the model documentation for these packages for more information.

</dsc>

<pkx id="TQpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" >
<dsc reserve="169" >The â€œAnalysis Elementsâ€? package contains the Analysis Classes.
Instances of the Analysis Classes appear in the diagrams in the &quot;Analysis Use-Case Realizations&quot; package.</dsc>
<nam>Analysis Elements</nam>
<mnd>
<RMS:LRF id="TgpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
</mnd>
<owd>
<dgx id="TgpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" >
<tvs>
<RMS:LRF id="UwtADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
<RMS:LRF id="WwtADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
<RMS:LRF id="MAxADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
</tvs>
<dsc reserve="780" >The contents of the â€œAnalysis Elementsâ€? package are shown above.  

In addition to Analysis Classes, packages can be defined within the â€œAnalysis Elementsâ€? package to further partition the contained Analysis Classes. 
In this template, a separate &quot;Key Abstractions&quot; package has been defined to contain the key abstractions of the system.

Such additional partitioning is optional, especially if a separate Analysis Model is not to be maintained.  In such cases, the Analysis Classes can be considered â€œtransientâ€? (i.e., they only exist until they evolve into design elements), so their organization is not considered critical.  One possible exception are the key abstraction Analysis Classes.  

View the &quot;Key Abstractions&quot; package model documentation for more information.</dsc>

<pkx id="egpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" >
<dsc reserve="650" >The â€œKey Abstractionsâ€? package contains the Analysis Classes that are considered to represent the key abstractions of the system.  This package is optional.  An alternative is to represent the key abstractions on a class diagram in the â€œAnalysis Elementsâ€? package.  However, creating a separate package provides a more explicit categorization of Analysis Classes as key abstractions.  In fact, even if a separate Analysis Model is not maintained in its entirety, some projects may choose to maintain the key abstraction Analysis Classes. In such cases, defining a separate package to contain the Analysis Classes that are to be maintained is helpful.</dsc>
<nam>Key Abstractions</nam>
<mnd>
<RMS:LRF id="ewpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
</mnd>

<pkx id="lQpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" >
<dsc reserve="207" >The â€œAnalysis Use-Case Realizationsâ€? package contains the analysis-level Use-Case Realizations, which describe how Use Cases are performed in terms of the Analysis Classes in the â€œAnalysis Elementsâ€? package.</dsc>
<nam>Analysis Use-Case Realizations</nam>
<mnd>
<RMS:LRF id="lgpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
</mnd>
<owd>
<dgx id="lgpADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" >
<tvs>
<RMS:LRF id="UwtADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
<RMS:LRF id="WwtADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
<RMS:LRF id="MAxADJ+o2BGY5AANVpPQ2w" />
</tvs>
<dsc reserve="402" >The analysis-level Use-Case Realizations describe how the Use Cases are performed in terms of the Analysis Classes in the â€œAnalysis Elementsâ€? package. 

Each of the analysis Use-Case Realizations realizes a Use Case in the Use-Case Model, has the same name as that Use Case, and should have the same structure.  For more information, see the model documentation for &quot;Analysis Use-Case Realization 1&quot;.</dsc>

<dsc reserve="566" >All analysis-level Use-Case Realizations should have the same structure.  This structure is easier to view in the Model Explorer.  Thus, right click on &quot;Analysis Use-Case Realization 1&quot; in the above diagram and click on &quot;Select in Model Explorer&quot;.

There is a &quot;Participants&quot; diagram and a set of &quot;flow&quot; interaction instances (&quot;Basic Flow&quot;, &quot;Alternate Flow 1&quot;, and &quot;Alternate Flow 2&quot;).  There should be one interaction instance for each significant use-case flow of events.  

For information on these model elements and diagrams, see their model documentation.
</dsc>

<dsc reserve="566" >&quot;Flow&quot; interaction instances contain sequence diagrams that describe the interactions of the Analysis Classes during the Use Case's flows of events. There should be one &quot;flow&quot; interaction instance for each significant use-case flow of events. 

For example, this interaction instance, &quot;Basic Flow&quot;, contains the sequence diagram that describes the interaction of the Analysis Classes during the Use Case's basic flow of events.

See the model documentation for the &quot;Basic Flow&quot; diagram for more information on the &quot;flow&quot; interaction instance sequence diagrams.
</dsc>
<nam>Basic Flow</nam>
